# Using AI Tools for UX Design

> While professionals across virtually every industry and field may be curious—or nervous—about the increasing influence of artificial intelligence, there are many tools now available that can help you streamline your processes and work more efficiently. In this course, explore how AI-powered tools can help improve the process of UX design with expert Eric Nordquist. Eric examines tools like Midourn

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design) | 1h 57m | Intermediate | 37K learners

#### [AI tools for UX designers](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/ai-tools-for-ux-designers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/ai-tools-for-ux-designers?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Eric Nordquist] Are you a UX designer that's feeling a bit nervous about the future of your role with all these new AI tools being released?
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/ai-tools-for-ux-designers?u=76281980&t=7)** We will complete a branding exercise for a new business using tools such as [[Midjourney]], [[DALL-E]] 2 and [[ChatGPT]] to create some website concepts, image icon assets, brand colors, and placeholder text content.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/ai-tools-for-ux-designers?u=76281980&t=23)** After completing this course, you will feel confident that you can successfully continue building on your skills using AI tools to ensure you are knowledgeable on the next generation of tools that can help you be a more efficient UX designer.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/ai-tools-for-ux-designers?u=76281980&t=38)** My name is Eric Nordquist and I've worked as a UX professional for 20 years managing teams at large corporations as well as teaching future students as a professor.

#### [Expectations](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Before we get started on our project, I wanted to set the expectations for the course.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=5)** I'm assuming you're an experienced UI/UX designer with a lot of knowledge using design tools.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=10)** I will be using [[Figma (Software)|Figma]] throughout this course to store the outputs from the AI tools we'll be working with, but we won't be doing any actual work inside of Figma.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=19)** So feel free to use Sketch or another design tool if you're more comfortable with those.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=24)** I've created a fictional client so we can simulate an actual project, but I will stop short in this course of actually building out the client's website.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=32)** I assume you already know how to build out a website concept, so I will focus only on how to leverage AI tools to create all the assets needed for the designing of the website.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=43)** Also, keep in mind the course will cover several AI tools, so it's not meant to be a deep dive into any one tool, but rather an overview of how we can use these tools in our day-to-day workflow as UX designers.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=58)** Many of the tools we will be reviewing are still in early beta phase, as this whole AI tool space is expanding very quickly right now.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=67)** We won't use every tool, but I will walk you through how to use the most popular tools, then I'll briefly make you aware of alternatives so that you can make sure to keep track of them as they progress.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=79)** I won't be posting any exercise files with this course since the content you generate as you follow this course will not be identical to what I'm creating.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=87)** That's because of the inherent randomness of using these AI tools.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=91)** For example, if you ask an AI tool for a picture of a coffee cup sitting on a desk and I ask it the same thing, we will get different results.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=99)** So, as you follow along in the course, you're not going to be matching my output identically.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=105)** What we're going to be doing is going through the process of using these tools during the different steps of our concepting of this website.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=112)** You'll be doing it on your own and tweaking your own output.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=115)** So the goal of the course is not to match my image assets, or any of the output I create.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/expectations?u=76281980&t=120)** The goal is to go through the process and understand how to use the tools moving forward on your own.

### 1. Project Overview

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [Client's ask](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So before we dive right in and start looking at tools and seeing how they can help us be more efficient, I wanted to go over the outline a little bit of the hypothetical project I've set up.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=10)** I always found that I learn better whenever I have a bit of a simulated stress of a customer or a client or a project manager that I'm trying to deliver for.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=20)** So I try and set up as real a situation as it would be in real life.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=24)** So for this course, I've created a hypothetical client or customer that's a local coffee shop.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=30)** Basically we have a small cafe or coffee shop.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=34)** They just bought a building in town, wherever it is that we live, and they're looking for someone to help them make a website.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=41)** Now, they're in the very early stages.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=43)** They just bought their building.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=44)** They do not have a name, they do not have a logo, and there's no colors, no branding guidelines, anything like that.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=51)** So what I did was sit down with them and have just a quick client kickoff to try and understand more about what's going on.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=58)** So, like I mentioned, background information about their business.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=61)** They're just a small shop in town, just purchased a building and they need help.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=65)** So I probed with a series of questions to try and ask, you know, tease out something about what it is they want, asking them if they have any names, logos, do they have any ideas, have they sketched anything on a napkin?.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=78)** Is there any coffee shops they've seen that they really like, any restaurants, any colors, anything.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=85)** And I couldn't get anything out of the client in relation to that.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=89)** So, of course, it's always a bit of a bummer.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=91)** A little bit harder for us 'cause it means we have no limits on what we can do, which then of course means we could work forever.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=98)** So this is actually a pretty good project for us using these new artificial intelligent tools because it's going to really show the effectiveness of how quick they can help us concept some things out.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=108)** So the initial ask from the client, they're just wanting a few rough concepts so that they can approve before we move forward in a particular direction.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=117)** So typically we would have to go off and gather a bunch of reference material and start creating some high-level concepts that would vary pretty drastically early on so that we can see which one resonates most.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=129)** Then we would go in that direction and keep tightening up that design a little bit further.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=133)** But overall for us, the goal is simply a direction on a website.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=137)** So we're not going to build out the full website for them, we're just going to give them a direction.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=141)** We're going to help them some with their verbiage, their content, tone of voice, so kind of branding guidelines, colors and fonts.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=147)** And then let's see if we can also help them out a little bit with a logo as well.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=151)** So while I've set this up more as if we were a freelance designer who now has a client, if that's not resonating with you, you can, of course, very easily think of this also as you are in your corporate job and project manager, program manager, marketing manager has come to you with a early idea and they're just wanting you to help them flush that idea out further.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=172)** So the same kind of efficiencies will apply here with the tools we're going to learn.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/client-s-ask?u=76281980&t=176)** All right, so now that we have an overview of kind of what this hypothetical project is we're going to be working on throughout the course, let's go ahead and get started.

### 2. Creating Concepts Using Text-to-Image AI

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [Introduction to text-to-image AI apps](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] I wanted to start by giving a brief overview of the tools that we have at our disposal when we start talking about text-to-image generators.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=8)** Now, you may also hear these be called AI art generators, but we'll discuss them as text-to-image generators.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=16)** Right, and if we think about that name text-to-image, it's hinting at the fact that we are going to be interacting with these tools via text.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=24)** Right, our creativity is going to come from how we [[Microsoft Word|word]] the prompts inside of these tools.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=30)** What words we use, and how we frame those words are going to drastically distinguish the type of artwork that comes out of it or the type of imagery.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=40)** Right, so when you hear about [[Prompt Engineering]], what we're talking about for the level that we're at is how we're typing that prompt in order to tell the tool what it is we're looking to get out of the tool.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=51)** So that's going to be the key thing that you need to practice and play with, and also where your creativity can shine.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=57)** So let's start looking at some of the top players inside the text-to-image generator space.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=62)** The first one I have open is [[Midjourney]].
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=64)** [Midjourney.com](https://Midjourney.com).
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=66)** That's a tool we're going to be using the most throughout this course.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=69)** It's the one I've found the most capable, currently.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=71)** Midjourney does a really good job of creating photorealistic images, although it can also create other aspects as well, which you'll find out in this course.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=79)** But Midjourney is a really good one, been around forever.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=82)** It's definitely one of the top tools for sure.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=84)** So [midjourney.com](https://midjourney.com).
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=86)** And the second one, which I think is a close second behind Midjourney, depending again on what type of assets you're trying to create because all these tools [[Microsoft Excel|excel]] at creating different types of artwork.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=96)** They're all based on different models on the backend.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=98)** So as you type in your prompts, you get different things from each of these tools.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=102)** You're going to play around with each of the tools and see which one gives you the type of imagery that you're looking for.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=107)** And you're going to have to vary it also.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=108)** Right, maybe for one project you need something photorealistic, so you use Midjourney.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=113)** Maybe for another project, it's more Illustrator or paint-based, so maybe [[DALL-E]] does a better job.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=118)** But DALL-E too is the second one.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=119)** It's created by a company called OpenAI, which you've probably heard of because they also made [[ChatGPT]], which we'll be using in this course as well.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=126)** So for me, DALL-E, is what I use a lot for icons and some illustrative stuff.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=131)** We'll get into that tool as well.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=133)** And then these other three we're not going to get into in the course, but I want to go ahead and just make you aware of them.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=137)** The other one closely following Midjourney and DALL-E is by [stability.ai](https://stability.ai), and it is called [[Stable Diffusion]].
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=145)** Stable Diffusion is just as powerful as Midjourney and DALL-E 2, so make sure you keep that on your radar and look into that.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=153)** I know Stable Diffusion, to me, is being used by a lot of artists that are creating artwork.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=158)** So it allows super, super granular, fine-tuning, but it's also a little bit more difficult as far as how you interact with a tool.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=165)** It's a little more setting up, but for our use, the additional kind of granularity isn't worth the necessary setup.

> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=171)** So we won't be using [stability.ai](https://stability.ai)'s tool today.

> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/introduction-to-text-to-image-ai-apps?u=76281980&t=175)** And the next one we have is recently released by Twitter, now known as X, and it is Grok.

> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/midjourney-uploading-reference-photos?u=76281980&t=340)** So now we can see from Midjourney how feeding Midjourney reference material will drastically improve the results we get in a given direction.
>
> **[5:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/midjourney-uploading-reference-photos?u=76281980&t=349)** So if we're looking for a certain style, a certain color palette, illustrative or photorealistic, leveraging the ability to upload or link a reference image to Midjourney is a huge benefit.

#### [Creating font pairing using Fontjoy and other tools in Obsidian](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/creating-font-pairing-using-fontjoy-and-other-tools-in-obsidian?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>

>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=10)** We also used several other tools to create our brand colors, our font pairings, and some logos.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=17)** My hope is that you now feel more empowered by these AI tools in how you can start to fit them into your daily workflows to increase your efficiency versus looking at them as something that will take your job.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=29)** As you saw throughout this course, there is still a long way to go before the output of these tools can replace the work we do as UX design professionals.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=40)** A good next step would be for you to continue studying how to write prompts for all the major tools we reviewed so you're better able to tailor the output to your needs and also to really start to include your creativity into this process.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=56)** These tools are super robust and those that master [[Prompt Engineering]] will be leaders in this space.

> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/using-ai-tools-for-ux-design/wrapping-up?u=76281980&t=63)** You should feel confident now in your ability to quickly create concepts, image and icon assets, as well as leverage smaller tools to help increase the resolution and vectorizing of images and that you feel you will be completely successful as a UX designer surrounded by this new age of AI tools.
